<p><b>Tulagi</b>, less commonly known as <b>Tulaghi</b>, is a small <a href="/wiki/Island" title="Island">island</a> (5.5&#160;km by 1&#160;km, area 2,08&#160;km²) in <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>, just off the south coast of <a href="/wiki/Nggela_Islands" title="Nggela Islands">Ngella Sule</a>. The town of the same name on the island (pop. 1,750) was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/British_Solomon_Islands" title="British Solomon Islands">British Solomon Islands Protectorate</a> from 1896 to 1942 and is today the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Province,_Solomon_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Province, Solomon Islands">Central Province</a>.  The capital of what is now the state of <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a> moved to <a href="/wiki/Honiara" title="Honiara">Honiara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal" title="Guadalcanal">Guadalcanal</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_campaign" title="Solomon Islands campaign">World War II</a>.
</p><p>The island was originally chosen by the British as a comparatively isolated and healthier alternative to the disease-ridden larger islands of the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_archipelago" class="mw-redirect" title="Solomon Islands archipelago">Solomon Islands archipelago</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tulagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first recorded sighting by Europeans was by the Spanish expedition of <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_de_Menda%C3%B1a_de_Neira" title="Álvaro de Mendaña de Neira">Álvaro de Mendaña</a> on 16 April 1568. More precisely the sighting was due to a local voyage done by a small boat, in the accounts the <a href="/wiki/Brigantine" title="Brigantine">brigantine</a> <i>Santiago</i>, commanded by <i><a href="/wiki/Maestre_de_Campo" class="mw-redirect" title="Maestre de Campo">Maestre de Campo</a></i> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pedro_Ortega_Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pedro Ortega Valencia (page does not exist)">Pedro Ortega Valencia</a> and having <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hern%C3%A1n_Gallego&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hernán Gallego (page does not exist)">Hernán Gallego</a> as pilot.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tulagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japanese</a> occupied Tulagi on May 3, 1942, with the intention of establishing a <a href="/wiki/Seaplane" title="Seaplane">seaplane</a> base nearby (see <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Tulagi_landing_(1942)" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Tulagi landing (1942)">Japanese Tulagi landing</a>).  The ships in Tulagi harbor were raided by planes from <a href="/wiki/USS_Yorktown_(CV-5)" title="USS Yorktown (CV-5)">USS&#160;<i>Yorktown</i></a> the following day in a prelude to the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Coral_Sea" title="Battle of the Coral Sea">Battle of the Coral Sea</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">U.S.</a> forces, primarily the 1st <a href="/wiki/Marine_Raiders" title="Marine Raiders">Marine Raiders</a>, landed on August 7 and captured Tulagi as part of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Watchtower" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Watchtower">Operation Watchtower</a> after a day of hard fighting.
</p><p>After its capture by <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">Naval</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">Marine forces</a>, the island hosted a squadron of <a href="/wiki/PT_boat" title="PT boat">PT boats</a> for a year which included LTJG <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Motor_Torpedo_Boat_PT-109" class="mw-redirect" title="Motor Torpedo Boat PT-109">PT-109</a>, as well as other ancillary facilities. A small 20-bed dispensary was operated on Tulagi until its closure in 1946. The island also formed part of <a href="/wiki/Purvis_Bay" title="Purvis Bay">Purvis Bay</a>, which hosted many US Navy ships during 1942 and 1943.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Postwar">Postwar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tulagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Postwar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The present-day Tulagi has a <a href="/wiki/Fishing_fleet" title="Fishing fleet">fishing fleet</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scuba_diving">Scuba diving</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tulagi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Scuba diving">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Tulagi offers some excellent <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba diving</a>. The wrecks of <a href="/wiki/USS_Aaron_Ward_(DD-483)" title="USS Aaron Ward (DD-483)">USS <i>Aaron Ward</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Kanawha_(AO-1)" title="USS Kanawha (AO-1)">USS <i>Kanawha</i></a>, and <a href="/wiki/HMNZS_Moa_(T233)" title="HMNZS Moa (T233)">HMNZS <i>Moa</i></a> are close by, and the wrecks of <a href="/wiki/Ironbottom_Sound" title="Ironbottom Sound">Ironbottom Sound</a> are not much further off, to the south and west.  These three ships were all sunk in the same Japanese naval air raid, part of the Operation "I" on April 7, 1943. The <a href="/wiki/USS_Aaron_Ward_(DD-483)" title="USS Aaron Ward (DD-483)"><i>Ward</i></a>  lies upright and intact, its deck replete with artifacts, on a sandy bottom at 70 metres (230 feet), about 20 metres (66 feet) deeper than one can safely dive on <a href="/wiki/Breathing_gas" title="Breathing gas">compressed air</a>. 
</p><p>Tulagi is developing a <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism industry</a> based on scuba.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
